<p class="p1"><span class="s1"></span><br></p>
<p class="p2"><span class="s1"></span><br></p>
<h2 style="margin: 0.0px 0.0px 10.0px 0.0px; line-height: 33.0px; font: 30.0px 'Helvetica Neue'; color: #262626; -webkit-text-stroke: #262626"><span class="s1">Introduction to deep learning</span></h2>
<p class="p4"><span class="s1">Neueste Einreichungsbewertung</span></p>
<p class="p5"><span class="s1">100%</span></p>
<p class="p6"><span class="s1">1.</span></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s1">Frage 1</span></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s1">What does the analogy ‚ÄúAI is the new electricity‚Äù refer to?</span></p>
<p class="p8"><span class="s2"><b>1 / 1 Punkten</b></span></p>
<p class="p9"><span class="s1"><b></b></span><br></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s1">Through the ‚Äúsmart grid‚Äù, AI is delivering a new wave of electricity.<span class="Apple-converted-space">¬†</span></span></p>
<p class="p9"><span class="s1"><b></b></span><br></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s1">AI is powering personal devices in our homes and offices, similar to electricity.</span></p>
<p class="p9"><span class="s1"><b></b></span><br></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s1">Similar to electricity starting about 100 years ago, AI is transforming multiple industries.<span class="Apple-converted-space">¬†</span></span></p>
<p class="p9"><span class="s1"><b></b></span><br></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s1">AI runs on computers and is thus powered by electricity, but it is letting computers do things not possible before.<span class="Apple-converted-space">¬†</span></span></p>
<p class="p10"><span class="s3">Check</span></p>
<p class="p11"><span class="s3">Richtig</span></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s3">Yes. AI is transforming many fields from the car industry to agriculture to supply-chain...</span></p>
<p class="p6"><span class="s1">2.</span></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s1">Frage 2</span></p>
<p class="p12"><span class="s1">Which of these are reasons for Deep Learning recently taking off? (Check the three options that apply.)</span></p>
<p class="p1"><span class="s1"></span><br></p>
<p class="p8"><span class="s2"><b>1 / 1 Punkten</b></span></p>
<p class="p9"><span class="s1"><b></b></span><br></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s1">We have access to a lot more computational power.<span class="Apple-converted-space">¬†</span></span></p>
<p class="p10"><span class="s3">Check</span></p>
<p class="p11"><span class="s3">Richtig</span></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s3">Yes! The development of hardware, perhaps especially GPU computing, has significantly improved deep learning algorithms' performance.<span class="Apple-converted-space">¬†</span></span></p>
<p class="p9"><span class="s1"><b></b></span><br></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s1">Neural Networks are a brand new field.<span class="Apple-converted-space">¬†</span></span></p>
<p class="p9"><span class="s1"><b></b></span><br></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s1">Deep learning has resulted in significant improvements in important applications such as online advertising, speech recognition, and image recognition.<span class="Apple-converted-space">¬†</span></span></p>
<p class="p10"><span class="s3">Check</span></p>
<p class="p11"><span class="s3">Richtig</span></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s3">These were all examples discussed in lecture 3.<span class="Apple-converted-space">¬†</span></span></p>
<p class="p9"><span class="s1"><b></b></span><br></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s1">We have access to a lot more data.</span></p>
<p class="p10"><span class="s3">Check</span></p>
<p class="p11"><span class="s3">Richtig</span></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s3">Yes! The digitalization of our society has played a huge role in this.</span></p>
<p class="p6"><span class="s1">3.</span></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s1">Frage 3</span></p>
<p class="p12"><span class="s1">Recall this diagram of iterating over different ML ideas. Which of the statements below are true? (Check all that apply.)</span></p>
<p class="p13"><span class="s1"><img src="file:///FalVl3ygEeegaQ4NYTdESg_7a0184575b8bdc47f8c3f29601302cb8_Screen-Shot-2017-08-08-at-6.13.59-PM.png" alt="FalVl3ygEeegaQ4NYTdESg_7a0184575b8bdc47f8c3f29601302cb8_Screen-Shot-2017-08-08-at-6.13.59-PM.png"></span></p>
<p class="p1"><span class="s1"></span><br></p>
<p class="p8"><span class="s2"><b>1 / 1 Punkten</b></span></p>
<p class="p9"><span class="s1"><b></b></span><br></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s1">Being able to try out ideas quickly allows deep learning engineers to iterate more quickly.<span class="Apple-converted-space">¬†</span></span></p>
<p class="p10"><span class="s3">Check</span></p>
<p class="p11"><span class="s3">Richtig</span></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s3">Yes, as discussed in Lecture 4.<span class="Apple-converted-space">¬†</span></span></p>
<p class="p9"><span class="s1"><b></b></span><br></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s1">Faster computation can help speed up how long a team takes to iterate to a good idea.<span class="Apple-converted-space">¬†</span></span></p>
<p class="p10"><span class="s3">Check</span></p>
<p class="p11"><span class="s3">Richtig</span></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s3">Yes, as discussed in Lecture 4.<span class="Apple-converted-space">¬†</span></span></p>
<p class="p9"><span class="s1"><b></b></span><br></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s1">It is faster to train on a big dataset than a small dataset.<span class="Apple-converted-space">¬†</span></span></p>
<p class="p9"><span class="s1"><b></b></span><br></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s1">Recent progress in deep learning algorithms has allowed us to train good models faster (even without changing the CPU/GPU hardware).<span class="Apple-converted-space">¬†</span></span></p>
<p class="p10"><span class="s3">Check</span></p>
<p class="p11"><span class="s3">Richtig</span></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s3">Yes. For example, we discussed how switching from sigmoid to ReLU activation functions allows faster training.<span class="Apple-converted-space">¬†</span></span></p>
<p class="p6"><span class="s1">4.</span></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s1">Frage 4</span></p>
<p class="p12"><span class="s1">When an experienced deep learning engineer works on a new problem, they can usually use insight from previous problems to train a good model on the first try, without needing to iterate multiple times through different models. True/False?</span></p>
<p class="p1"><span class="s1"></span><br></p>
<p class="p8"><span class="s2"><b>1 / 1 Punkten</b></span></p>
<p class="p9"><span class="s1"><b></b></span><br></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s1">True</span></p>
<p class="p9"><span class="s1"><b></b></span><br></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s1">False</span></p>
<p class="p10"><span class="s3">Check</span></p>
<p class="p11"><span class="s3">Richtig</span></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s3">Yes. Finding the characteristics of a model is key to have good performance. Although experience can help, it requires multiple iterations to build a good model.</span></p>

<p class="p6"><span class="s1">6.</span></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s1">Frage 6</span></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s1">Images for cat recognition is an example of ‚Äústructured‚Äù data, because it is represented as a structured array in a computer. True/False?</span></p>
<p class="p8"><span class="s2"><b>1 / 1 Punkten</b></span></p>
<p class="p9"><span class="s1"><b></b></span><br></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s1">True</span></p>
<p class="p9"><span class="s1"><b></b></span><br></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s1">False</span></p>
<p class="p10"><span class="s3">Check</span></p>
<p class="p11"><span class="s3">Richtig</span></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s3">Yes. Images for cat recognition is an example of ‚Äúunstructured‚Äù data.</span></p>
<p class="p6"><span class="s1">7.</span></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s1">Frage 7</span></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s1">A demographic dataset with statistics on different cities' population, GDP per capita, economic growth is an example of ‚Äúunstructured‚Äù data because it contains data coming from different sources. True/False?</span></p>
<p class="p8"><span class="s2"><b>1 / 1 Punkten</b></span></p>
<p class="p9"><span class="s1"><b></b></span><br></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s1">True</span></p>
<p class="p9"><span class="s1"><b></b></span><br></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s1">False</span></p>
<p class="p10"><span class="s3">Check</span></p>
<p class="p11"><span class="s3">Richtig</span></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s3">A demographic dataset with statistics on different cities' population, GDP per capita, economic growth is an example of ‚Äústructured‚Äù data by opposition to image, audio or text datasets.</span></p>
<p class="p6"><span class="s1">8.</span></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s1">Frage 8</span></p>
<p class="p12"><span class="s1">Why is an RNN (Recurrent Neural Network) used for machine translation, say translating English to French? (Check all that apply.)</span></p>
<p class="p14"><span class="s1"></span><br></p>
<p class="p1"><span class="s1"></span><br></p>
<p class="p8"><span class="s2"><b>1 / 1 Punkten</b></span></p>
<p class="p9"><span class="s1"><b></b></span><br></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s1">It can be trained as a supervised learning problem.<span class="Apple-converted-space">¬†</span></span></p>
<p class="p10"><span class="s3">Check</span></p>
<p class="p11"><span class="s3">Richtig</span></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s3">Yes. We can train it on many pairs of sentences x (English) and y (French).<span class="Apple-converted-space">¬†</span></span></p>
<p class="p9"><span class="s1"><b></b></span><br></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s1">It is strictly more powerful than a Convolutional Neural Network (CNN).<span class="Apple-converted-space">¬†</span></span></p>
<p class="p9"><span class="s1"><b></b></span><br></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s1">It is applicable when the input/output is a sequence (e.g., a sequence of words).<span class="Apple-converted-space">¬†</span></span></p>
<p class="p10"><span class="s3">Check</span></p>
<p class="p11"><span class="s3">Richtig</span></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s3">Yes. An RNN can map from a sequence of english words to a sequence of french words.<span class="Apple-converted-space">¬†</span></span></p>
<p class="p9"><span class="s1"><b></b></span><br></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s1">RNNs represent the recurrent process of Idea-&gt;Code-&gt;Experiment-&gt;Idea-&gt;....<span class="Apple-converted-space">¬†</span></span></p>
<p class="p6"><span class="s1">9.</span></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s1">Frage 9</span></p>
<p class="p12"><span class="s1">In this diagram which we hand-drew in lecture, what do the horizontal axis (x-axis) and vertical axis (y-axis) represent?<span class="Apple-converted-space">¬†</span></span></p>
<p class="p13"><span class="s1"><img src="file:///JP--G3ooEeeJIwrF5BVsIg_b60d752c05bec0881d8ca08cfc2646d2_Screen-Shot-2017-08-05-at-2.30.09-PM.png" alt="JP--G3ooEeeJIwrF5BVsIg_b60d752c05bec0881d8ca08cfc2646d2_Screen-Shot-2017-08-05-at-2.30.09-PM.png"></span></p>
<p class="p14"><span class="s1"></span><br></p>
<p class="p1"><span class="s1"></span><br></p>
<p class="p8"><span class="s2"><b>1 / 1 Punkten</b></span></p>
<p class="p9"><span class="s1"><b></b></span><br></p>
<ul class="ul1">
  <li class="li16"><span class="s4"></span><span class="s1">x-axis is the performance of the algorithm</span></li>
  <li class="li16"><span class="s4"></span><span class="s1">y-axis (vertical axis) is the amount of data.</span></li>
</ul>
<p class="p9"><span class="s1"><b></b></span><br></p>
<ul class="ul1">
  <li class="li16"><span class="s4"></span><span class="s1">x-axis is the amount of data</span></li>
  <li class="li16"><span class="s4"></span><span class="s1">y-axis is the size of the model you train.<span class="Apple-converted-space">¬†</span></span></li>
</ul>
<p class="p9"><span class="s1"><b></b></span><br></p>
<ul class="ul1">
  <li class="li16"><span class="s4"></span><span class="s1">x-axis is the input to the algorithm</span></li>
  <li class="li16"><span class="s4"></span><span class="s1">y-axis is outputs.</span></li>
</ul>
<p class="p9"><span class="s1"><b></b></span><br></p>
<ul class="ul1">
  <li class="li16"><span class="s4"></span><span class="s1">x-axis is the amount of data</span></li>
  <li class="li16"><span class="s4"></span><span class="s1">y-axis (vertical axis) is the performance of the algorithm.</span></li>
</ul>
<p class="p10"><span class="s3">Check</span></p>
<p class="p11"><span class="s3">Richtig</span></p>
<p class="p2"><span class="s1"></span><br></p>
<p class="p6"><span class="s1">10.</span></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s1">Frage 10</span></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s1">Assuming the trends described in the previous question's figure are accurate (and hoping you got the axis labels right), which of the following are true? (Check all that apply.)</span></p>
<p class="p8"><span class="s2"><b>1 / 1 Punkten</b></span></p>
<p class="p9"><span class="s1"><b></b></span><br></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s1">Increasing the size of a neural network generally does not hurt an algorithm‚Äôs performance, and it may help significantly.</span></p>
<p class="p10"><span class="s3">Check</span></p>
<p class="p11"><span class="s3">Richtig</span></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s3">Yes. According to the trends in the figure above, big networks usually perform better than small networks.<span class="Apple-converted-space">¬†</span></span></p>
<p class="p9"><span class="s1"><b></b></span><br></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s1">Increasing the training set size generally does not hurt an algorithm‚Äôs performance, and it may help significantly.<span class="Apple-converted-space">¬†</span></span></p>
<p class="p10"><span class="s3">Check</span></p>
<p class="p11"><span class="s3">Richtig</span></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s3">Yes. Bringing more data to a model is almost always beneficial.</span></p>
<p class="p9"><span class="s1"><b></b></span><br></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s1">Decreasing the training set size generally does not hurt an algorithm‚Äôs performance, and it may help significantly.</span></p>
<p class="p9"><span class="s1"><b></b></span><br></p>
<p class="p7"><span class="s1">Decreasing the size of a neural network generally does not hurt an algorithm‚Äôs performance, and it may help significantly.</span></p>
